  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bdce19f0-18e7-4830-b197-034195547e2e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1277737991?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren Kammerdiener" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren Kammerdiener" href="/user/show/34240268-lauren-kammerdiener">Lauren Kammerdiener</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34240268-lauren-kammerdiener?shelf=releases-2016">releases-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34240268-lauren-kammerdiener?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34240268-lauren-kammerdiener?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34240268-lauren-kammerdiener?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34240268-lauren-kammerdiener?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34240268-lauren-kammerdiener?shelf=sequel-series">sequel-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34240268-lauren-kammerdiener?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34240268-lauren-kammerdiener?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1277737991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12230366738383508598"><blockquote>
  <i>"I'm telling you, Eady, wars and treaties and even countries will all come and go. But your life is yours, singular and sacred, and you should be with the person who makes it feel that way every blessed second you live it."</i>
</blockquote><br/>First, I would like to thank every person who has liked or commented on this review in the past year or so. This much of a response is unheard of for me. Almost every day, a few more people like it, or someone else actively advocates for Kile or Erik and sends up a prayer </span>
  <span id="freeText12230366738383508598" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"I'm telling you, Eady, wars and treaties and even countries will all come and go. But your life is yours, singular and sacred, and you should be with the person who makes it feel that way every blessed second you live it."</i>
</blockquote><br />First, I would like to thank every person who has liked or commented on this review in the past year or so. This much of a response is unheard of for me. Almost every day, a few more people like it, or someone else actively advocates for Kile or Erik and sends up a prayer in the hopes America doesn't die. I've loved hearing everyone's predictions and hopes and dreams over the course of a year in waiting for what may or may not be the last of the Selection books, given the track record.<br /><br />Second, I wish it didn't have to end this way.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the original three Selection books. Sure, America could be annoying, but as long as you didn't take them too seriously, they were quick, fun reads.<br />But <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22918050.The_Heir__The_Selection___4_" title="The Heir (The Selection, #4) by Kiera Cass" rel="nofollow noopener">The Heir</a> was not a good read for me, for reasons I have already stated in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1034643060" rel="nofollow noopener">my review</a>.<br /><br />So let's return to the points of improvement I listed here, the day I finished <i>The Heir</i>, in optimism for its sequel.<br /><br /><b>• Eadlyn to stop being spoiled and do something unselfish for her people.</b><br />By the end of the book, Eadlyn <i>says</i> she's learned her lesson, and that she's more aware of how privileged she is. But let's take a look.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>I stepped into the bath, noting there was no lavendar, no bubbles, no anything to sweeten the water. Eloise was quiet and fast, but she was no Neena. I sighed.</i>
</blockquote><br />So miss Princess--excuse me--<i>Queen</i> Eadlyn just can't enjoy her little bath without all its fluff, and she can't be bothered to just go and get it herself. That sounds like entitlement to me.<br />And does Eadlyn actually "do something unselfish for her people"?<br />Not really. She spends the entire book worrying about what they think of her rather than actually trying to help them. The two instances where she does try to reach out weren't even her idea. The first, the town hall meeting, was Marid's idea, and, as he points out, he was the one who had to save it in the end. The other instance, which never played out in the book, was Kile's idea for a throne room where the people could regularly come and talk to Eadlyn about their problems to get them fixed. This was what inspired Eadlyn <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[in the constitutional monarchy aspect, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> which was a nice touch, but, again, not really her idea.<br />An additional idea, proposed by again Kile, was the housing project. But instead of actively taking a hand in it herself, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Eadlyn banishes Kile from the palace and makes him do it on his own. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>• Eadlyn to actually interact with her people on any level.</b><br />See above.<br /><br /><b>• A good old-fashioned, knee-slappin, heck of a time ball.</b><br />Does the coronation ball count? I guess.<br /><br /><b>• Henri to find a cute maid to love.</b><br />I guess <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[it was really too much of a close call for Henri to have time "to find a maid to love." Maybe in book six. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>• Ahren to come back and have character development.</b><br />Oh, Ahren came back. But did he have character development?<br />I say not really. And I attribute it to the fact that Ahren and Eadlyn's relationship was never really solidified in <i>The Heir</i>. Eadlyn spent a good portion of this book lamenting over Ahren's departure, but it all felt very fake to me. Eadlyn in <i>The Crown</i> claimed she needed Ahren, that she relied on Ahren, but Eadlyn in <i>The Heir</i> hardly every interacted with him. She only every really mentioned Ahren in regard to his relationship with Camille. Therefore, it was hard to take their sudden closeness seriously.<br /><br /><b>• Either Erik or Kile winning the selection.</b><br />I think we all saw that one coming.<br /><br /><b>• Kile builds something cute to help Eadlyn.</b><br />Kile builds houses for those living in poverty, which is way better than building something for Eadlyn.<br /><br /><b>• Josie to get seriously told off by Eadlyn.</b><br />This one, in fact, has changed for me, and it's due to something someone commented on here a while back.<br />This person pointed out that it was always Eadlyn being unfair to Josie, not the other way around, and after thinking about it, I agree. It especially became apparent to me in some things Eadlyn said to Josie early on. While Josie was immature and annoying, she still never deserved to be treated so harshly by Eadlyn, because all she ever wanted was to be just like her.<br />So I was very pleased with the way things turned out between them. This was one point I was worried Kiera would drop the ball on, but she pulled through for me.<br /><br /><b>• Something exciting with Ean.</b><br />Something exciting most certainly did happen with Ean, but it was definitely not what I originally had in mind.<br />Ean's character quite honestly was disappointing for me. When Epic Reads was marketing <i>The Heir</i> they uploaded a bunch of videos that were mock interviews with some of the more important boys in the Selection. Ean was one of them, and his video, which portrayed him as a pompous little snake, got me really excited for some drama being thrown down.<br />But with the exception of Eadlyn's first meeting with him, he doesn't do anything at all in either books. He's always in the background. He might as well have been one of the boys Eadlyn sent home for all he's actually mentioned. I'm not even sure Eadlyn ever went on a date with him, and yet somehow he managed to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[make it to the Elite. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Kiera really dropped the ball on this one.<br /><br /><b>• America not to die.</b><br />Honestly, after thinking about it, I knew <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[there was a zero percent chance America was going to die. No way in heck was Kiera going to kill off a character so precious to her. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />In conclusion, as much regard as I have for Kiera as a person, and as much as I did like the original three books, these last two installments have caused everything to go to pieces. I'm not even sure there ever was a plot in these; most of it has been Eadlyn continually complaining about how "hard" her life is. What little drama exists feels fake and underdeveloped, and the world-building has gone so far under that we didn't even make it out of the palace in this book.<br />I mentioned the other day to a friend that reading this book has felt like reading fanfiction. It has all the plot holes, cheesiness, and enough of the original characters being married and having kids to give it that feel.<br />But, above all, Maxon Shreave will always and forever be life.<br /><br />------------------------------------------------<br /><br /><u>
  <b>PREREADING</b>
</u><br /><br />5/11/15<br />things i would like in this book:<br />- eadlyn to stop being spoiled &amp; do something unselfish for her people<br />- eadlyn to actually interact with her people on any level<br />- a good old-fashioned, knee-slappin, heck-of-a-time ball<br />- henri to find a cute maid to love<br />- ahren come back &amp; have character development<br />- either erik or kile winning the selection<br />- kile builds something cute to help eadlyn<br />- josie to get seriously told off by eadlyn<br />- something exciting with ean<br />- aMERICA NOT TO DIE ???</span>
  <a data-text-id="12230366738383508598" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1445600928" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1445600928" />
    <a title="Claudia Ramírez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13061577-claudia-ram-rez"><img alt="Claudia Ramírez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533869692p2/13061577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1445600928?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claudia Ramírez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claudia Ramírez" href="/user/show/13061577-claudia-ram-rez">Claudia Ramírez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13061577-claudia-ram-rez?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1445600928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12536819509685064943">THIS WILL BE A RANT.<br/><br/>It's a 2.5. The thing is... I enjoyed the book, but OMG, I'm just not buying anything that happened at the end! REALLY? So now Eadlyn gets to make whatever change she wants in the kingdom, she doesn't have to get it approved or even discussed with the council, nope, she just gives the surprise announcement and that's it! WHAT! That's not how a country works! Maybe Illéa has to respect everything she decides, but there will obviously be revolts! It was too simple! She was like</span>
  <span id="freeText12536819509685064943" style="display:none">THIS WILL BE A RANT.<br /><br />It's a 2.5. The thing is... I enjoyed the book, but OMG, I'm just not buying anything that happened at the end! REALLY? So now Eadlyn gets to make whatever change she wants in the kingdom, she doesn't have to get it approved or even discussed with the council, nope, she just gives the surprise announcement and that's it! WHAT! That's not how a country works! Maybe Illéa has to respect everything she decides, but there will obviously be revolts! It was too simple! She was like: YEAH I'M GONNA CHANGE THE WAY WE'VE BEEN RULING SINCE FOREVER, AND IT WILL BE AWESOME AND EVERYONE WILL BE HAPPY. NOPE.<br /><br />Also, I couldn't believe Maxon's decision! WHAT EVEN. I love Maxon but in this book he was just plain weak! I mean, I understand where he's coming from, but he can't just do what he did! OH WAIT, he can and HE DID. My God.<br /><br />What else? OHHH... let me talk about the person she chooses in the end: cliché cliché cliché! It was so obvious, and not because the romance was well-developed (because it was not) but because it was simply OBVIOUS. I mean, I like the boy, he was one of my favorites and one of my top choices, I just don't feel like the romance was believable. Suddenly they both were just like: OMG I LOVE YOU SO MUCH. It felt forced. Maxon's and America's story was BEAUTIFUL, so well-developed and believable and just perfect... but what we got in this book? Nope, not buying it.<br /><br />I have a lot of issues with this last installment, I think the series would've been fine with the first three books, I really loved them! But these last two? They were unnecesary. <br /><br />The things I liked? Hm... Henri, he was a cinnamon roll. I also liked Ean and Hale. Kile and Erik were also okay. The Elite boys won my heart at the end. And I also liked Eadlyn's choice, but I still feel it needed more romantic development.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12536819509685064943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1029162694" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1029162694" />
    <a title="Andreea Pop" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop"><img alt="Andreea Pop" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486663526p2/4858513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1029162694?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreea Pop" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreea Pop" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop">Andreea Pop</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=in-curand-in-romania">in-curand-in-romania</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=light-read">light-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=amazing-feelings">amazing-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=huge-character-development">huge-character-development</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=editura-leda">editura-leda</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=awesome-romance">awesome-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=great-parents">great-parents</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=swoon-worthy-characters">swoon-worthy-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1029162694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2653951639955191792">I'm gonna put it bluntly out there -- I did not like <i>The Heir</i>. I consider it one of my greatest literary disappointments, even if it has a relatively high rating (2.5 stars). So my expectations of <i>The Crown</i> were along the lines of <i>
  <b>'please be decent, please end quick and please be the last</b>
</i>'. Most fortunately though, <i>The Crown</i> brought back the love I felt for Kiera Cass's novels made of syrupy romance and dreamy sighs. Taking this into consideration, this review will resemble half an omen to t</span>
  <span id="freeText2653951639955191792" style="display:none">I'm gonna put it bluntly out there -- I did not like <i>The Heir</i>. I consider it one of my greatest literary disappointments, even if it has a relatively high rating (2.5 stars). So my expectations of <i>The Crown</i> were along the lines of <i>
  <b>'please be decent, please end quick and please be the last</b>
</i>'. Most fortunately though, <i>The Crown</i> brought back the love I felt for Kiera Cass's novels made of syrupy romance and dreamy sighs. Taking this into consideration, this review will resemble half an omen to this fifth installment and half a regret for what it did not come to fruition in its prequel, but only to highlight that this book exceeded my expectations and made me fall in love again with its world. <br /><br /><b>Unlike in The Heir</b>, I loved Eadlyn. She let go of her petty, egotistical, self-centered and vain antics in order to graciously transform into a more than capable young woman, leader and Queen. Yeah yeah, her character-development was speeded up to supersonic mode, but for once I didn't mind. She showed her thoughtfulness, her ambition, her intelligence and her strong personality. I admired the fact that she wants to do good by everyone around her and that she tries to mend her flaws. Regardless, she took a colossal departure from the stoic, stuck-up and artificial princess and became an oddly organic person, beautifully encapsulated through the integrity to her own heart and moral code. <br /><br /><b>Unlike in The Heir</b>, I didn't check the page count every two minutes to dreadfully discover there was still a long way to go until the finish. I was hooked and I read it easily, eager to see what's in store next. Tremendously enjoyable.<br /><br /><b>Unlike in The Heir</b>, I could connect to this bunch of boys. Instead of 35, there were only 6 left in the picture. Each of them (and here I'm talking about the ever-wonderful Hale, Kile, Ean, Henri and Erik) became amazing in their own way and right. <br /><br /><b>Unlike in The Heir</b>, I was actually surprised by some revelations. Marid and Brice, especially. And Maxon shocked me with his introspective tales. <br /><br /><b>Unlike in The Heir</b>, there were sweet relationships truly taking root. Deep, heartfelt friendships and dynamics that somehow evolved or appeared out of the blue only to fit the bill perfectly. Hale &amp; Eady. Hale &amp; Ean. Kile &amp; Eady. Erik &amp; Henri. Henri &amp; Eady. Josie &amp; Eady. Erik &amp; Eady. Brice &amp; Eady. Aspen &amp; Eady. <br /><br /><b>Unlike in The Heir</b>, I did not curse the decision to expand the series from the original trilogy. This closure, this grand second finale somehow tied up the loose ends of <i>The One</i> by making sure certain matters were addressed, political ones, LGBT ones, feminism ones and discriminatory ones. I finally understood that we couldn't leave things at how they were with the initial 'last book'. <br /><br /><b>Unlike in The Heir</b>, there was so much more of the young Maxon and America we all know. Seriously, all the glimpses into their fairy tale of a love story made my heart burst free. Maxon fretting over Mer and going borderline insane about her health was just too cute to handle. I'm glad they're happy and don't paint me foolish just because they're works of fiction, but in my mind they exist vividly and that's of the utmost importance. <br /><br /><b>Unlike in The Heir</b>, I wasn't constantly exhausted about the sad and ill-fated attempts at romance. This time, it all flourished naturally, because the focus was on the worthy and so a cute and amazing and awesome and lovely couple became canon. And speaking about that particular pairing, <b>I SHIP IT</b>. <br /><br /><b>Like The Heir</b>, don't expect this book to suddenly be a complex piece of literature, because surely it is not. It fits the style of the series, so it's one for the heart. It's 100% drama and teen romance. It's light. It's quick. It's totally YA. It's a great read for a spring afternoon. It's the kind of book that has you smiling, daydreaming and relaxing. <b>Unlike The Heir</b>. <br /><br /><b>Unlike the Heir</b>, <i>The Crown</i> was so much better. Infinitely better. I urge you to read it and see for yourself but I have faith that you'll love it bunches.<br /><br />Bye, Illea. For real now. <br /><br /><b>ENJOY! &lt;3 </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2653951639955191792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1412936059" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1412936059" />
    <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee"><img alt="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583262285p2/44137919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1412936059?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee">Mikee (ReadWithMikee)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1412936059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1335987097252655199"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462848728i/19051261._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>❝Finding a prince might mean kissing a lot of frogs. Or kicking a lot of frogs out of your house. Falling might mean running headfirst into something you always wanted. Or dipping your toe into something you've been scared your whole life. Happily ever after could be waiting in a field a mile wide.❞</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Rating: {★ ★ ★}<br/><br/>This was an okay ending to Eadlyn's part of the story in The Selection series. I was never really a fan of The Heir or Eadlyn like I was with The Selection and America. The </span>
  <span id="freeText1335987097252655199" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462848728i/19051261._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>❝Finding a prince might mean kissing a lot of frogs. Or kicking a lot of frogs out of your house. Falling might mean running headfirst into something you always wanted. Or dipping your toe into something you've been scared your whole life. Happily ever after could be waiting in a field a mile wide.❞</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Rating: {★ ★ ★}<br><br>This was an okay ending to Eadlyn's part of the story in The Selection series. I was never really a fan of The Heir or Eadlyn like I was with The Selection and America. The only reason I kept up with series after The One was because like many others, I was curious as to how everyone from the original trilogy grew up to be.<br><br>In all honesty, I should've just stopped after the third book. I don't want to say that The Heir and The Crown ruined The Selection for me but in a way it did. Instead of believing that everybody lived happily ever after once Maxon and America became king and queen and the caste system was eliminated, The Heir just sort of wipes that all away like happily ever after never even happened.<br><br>The One was such a bittersweet ending to a fun trilogy and The Crown with its 278 pages wasn't going to top it at all. Not by a long shot.<br><br>Nothing really happened in The Crown. To be honest, I thought this book was such a waste because nothing worthy or significant occurred. Sure, Eadlyn was less of a brat in this book but I'm still not very fond of her. On top of that, I thought it was absolutely preposterous that Maxon stepped down and gave up his title for Eadlyn to rule. That was by far the most unrealistic thing I've ever heard. No king is going to give up his duties because he was stressing about his queen's recovery or because he wants a normal life with his wife. Tough shit. That's like saying you're giving up being a parent because you're stressed out about having kids. Putting the fate of your whole country on Eadlyn? Good luck with that.<br><br>I also felt that the ending was really rushed. Too many things were resolved too quickly and too easily that added to the unrealism that I was struggling with.<br><br>On a positive note, I did enjoy the fact that Eadlyn's choice broke away from tradition. Was her choice a surprise? No, not really. From the very beginning, I knew it would come down to one specific person but I was curious as to how Kiera Cass was going to make it happen.<br><br>The Selection was one of the first series that got me into reading Young Adult. Though it is far from the best series out there, I will always have an attachment to the first three books of The Selection. The Heir and The Crown may not be up to par with Maxon and America's story, but I still found it bittersweet that The Selection is finally over for good.</span>

<div id="review_1247998940" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1247998940" />
    <a title="Beatrice Masaluñga" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga"><img alt="Beatrice Masaluñga" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603719912p2/4590441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1247998940?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beatrice Masaluñga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beatrice Masaluñga" href="/user/show/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga">Beatrice Masaluñga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1247998940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11017256961859981358"><b>Warning: My review contains spoilers. [ I added spoiler tags as many as I can... but you might guess what happens in the end based on my rating]</b><br/><br/><i>The Crown </i> continues as Eadlyn Schreave temporarily takes over Illea after the stressful things happened on the previous book. Taking the opportunity and experience is part of her lesson to fully become the next Queen. It's challenging on her part especially when The Selection is on going. Finding the right guy for her isn't easy. Whatever choice she mak</span>
  <span id="freeText11017256961859981358" style="display:none"><b>Warning: My review contains spoilers. [ I added spoiler tags as many as I can... but you might guess what happens in the end based on my rating]</b><br /><br /><i>The Crown </i> continues as Eadlyn Schreave temporarily takes over Illea after the stressful things happened on the previous book. Taking the opportunity and experience is part of her lesson to fully become the next Queen. It's challenging on her part especially when The Selection is on going. Finding the right guy for her isn't easy. Whatever choice she makes, she must follow what her heart speaks and unexpectedly changes everything.<br /><br />For me, the conclusion to this series is <b>bittersweet</b>. I'm going to be honest, I do like Kiera Cass but I have to say I'm disappointed with its ending. Like, really frustrated that I almost throw the book across the room because I'm holding to my thoughts and it ended not the way I expected or wanted. At the same time, I don't want to be selfish and one sided with the situation. I hope you'll understand my feeling of <i>when-your-ship-didn't-sail</i>. I'm still on denial stage and I'll get over this soon. I actually see it coming but I keep fighting the bad feeling, you know? Still, I am glad to see Eadlyn Schreave's character developed into a fine lady. She handled the situations maturely and earned my respect. <br /><br />Here I am, seeing the other perspective and tried to understand why it ended up like... <b>THAT</b>. I know some of you rooted for <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Erik/Eikko  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> to win and I respect that. I think he won because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[it's a rule breaker to the tradition, it's not a Maxon-America repeat, and somehow, his character shows that he's a genuine, humble, thoughtful and simple man. His character stood out in some way despite of being behind the spotlight. <br /><br />I'm sorry guys but I'm not convinced with this whole Erik - Eadlyn ship. I didn't feel the spark between them and it was sort of an insta-love. Unlike what Eadlyn shared with Kile, these two tried to like each other.. THEY'RE SLOWLY FALLING and the chemistry between them is so evident. I don't give a damn if it's predictable.. these two have the chemistry.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I have to vent out all of these. Apparently, this becomes my least favorite in the series. What can I do? Eadlyn's decision prevails and I should respect her choice. <br /><br /><b>Why my bet and others didn't win:</b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Kile - My bet. I am loyal to you no matter what. Among the other competitors, he knows Eadlyn the best. They've known each other for years. Majority, including myself are rooting for him. I guess it didn't sail because it's a Maxon-America repeat, predictable and boring. Well, I don't care. I want an alternate ending where Eadlyn and Kile ship SAIL. SADLY, THERE IS NO ALTERNATE ENDING. SHIP DOOMED FOREVER.<br /><br />Henri - obviously, communication barrier. a couple won't work out if there is a lack of communication.<br /><br />Hale - his charm fascinated me. He is like my back up bet. It seems he has a different type. ;)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Now, it's time to say goodbye to this series and I'm definitely going to miss it. I'm still looking forward to Kiera Cass's books in the future. Her writing style is really great and it effectively draws me into the story. Sadly, this book isn't for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11017256961859981358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1413865226" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1413865226" />
    <a title="Mariah of the Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29456303-mariah-of-the-night-court"><img alt="Mariah of the Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585943105p2/29456303.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1413865226?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mariah of the Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mariah of the Night Court" href="/user/show/29456303-mariah-of-the-night-court">Mariah of the Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1413865226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13500235645060181311"><b>SO DISAPPOINTED</b><br/><br/><b>***Contains Spoilers***</b><br/><br/>Kiera Cass seriously did not put that much effort in her last installment in the Selection series. The other books were great, especially the first three, but kind of lost their touch when Eadlyn was introduced. The Crown was so dry. It was like this...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464142791ra/19202137.gif' width='250' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Perfect comparison.<br/><br/>I really do not like Eadlyn as a character at all because she has no personality! All I hear out of her mouth is awkward, out of place dialogue that leaves me cringing. Everyone was telling </span>
  <span id="freeText13500235645060181311" style="display:none"><b>SO DISAPPOINTED</b><br><br><b>***Contains Spoilers***</b><br><br>Kiera Cass seriously did not put that much effort in her last installment in the Selection series. The other books were great, especially the first three, but kind of lost their touch when Eadlyn was introduced. The Crown was so dry. It was like this...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464142791ra/19202137.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Perfect comparison.<br><br>I really do not like Eadlyn as a character at all because she has no personality! All I hear out of her mouth is awkward, out of place dialogue that leaves me cringing. Everyone was telling her how great of a queen she'd be and I was there thinking, "Why would you guys happily trade Eadlyn in place of America and Maxon???". <b>SHE IS SUCH A FLAT CHARACTER.</b><br><br>There is seriously no character depth in this book. We don't get to dive into any of the suitors' backgrounds, and really, we don't get to hear that much from the suitors at all! No personalities, just smiling faces who constantly said things to Eadlyn like "I understand you completely", "I'm so sorry about your mom", and "You'll make a great queen". Okay, I realize that those are nice things to say about a girl, but when it comes to reading, that is so boring! Especially when <b>EVERY SINGLE GUY SAYS IT LIKE TEN TIMES.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464142489ra/19202119.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alright, let me just get it out. I hate it when characters are overly nice all the time and have no kind of dark side to them. Character flaws. Yeah, that's it. And backstories, which this book had none of. <b>CHARACTERS WHO ARE OVERLY NICE AND CHEERY ALL THE TIME ARE JUST SO BORING.</b> <br><br>Some conversations went sorta like this:<br><br>"Hello Eadlyn," said suitor.<br>"Hello," said Eadlyn.<br>"You look lovely today," said suitor.<br>"Oh wow thank you so much!" said Eadlyn.<br>"I'm sorry about your mom," said suitor.<br>"Aw thank you...she's starting to get better," said Eadlyn.<br>"That's good," said suitor.<br>"Yeah," said Eadlyn.<br>"Nice seeing you, bye," said suitor.<br>"Bye," said Eadlyn.<br><br><b>WASN'T THAT EXCITING OR WHAT.</b><br><br>Alright, I'm gonna spice up this scene for the fun of it, keeping the suitors lines, but changing Eadlyn's.<br><br>"Hello Eadlyn," said suitor.<br>"Hey ya fuck tard," said Eadlyn.<br>"You look lovely today," said suitor.<br>"Yeah I just took a shit on the crapper and thought of you" said Eadlyn.<br>"I'm sorry about your mom," said suitor.<br>"If I fucking hear that one more time I will stick my tiara up yo ass," said Eadlyn.<br>"That's good," said suitor.<br>"Bitch what the fuck did I just say," said Eadlyn.<br>"Nice seeing you, bye," said suitor.<br>"Stfu," said Eadlyn.<br><br><b>NOW THAT IS GOLD.</b><br><br>Alright, moving on. So apparently Hale and Ean are gay for each other. Before I go on, let me just say, I am not against homosexuality. But, when we found this out, I was so mad because of how random and out of place it was. Okay Kiera, so to make this faster to write, you're going to just have two of the elite fall for each other and get away with it so easily? When Hale told Eadlyn that he was in love with Ean I literally said "What the fuck?" while reading. Whatever, on to Erik.<br><br>I knew that Erik was going to be with Eadlyn in the end, like how obvious could it be? And it happened so fast. He's probably the least flat character out of all the characters (but he's still flat). Eadlyn literally chose to be with him in like the last five pages. <br><br>What really bothered me though, was how everyone was just fine and dandy with it. When Henri found out, he's like "Ok, I see the love. Be together. I love you guys, you're s'cute. Henri out."........okay Henri. And when Eadlyn announced to the millions of viewers watching the broadcast that she was going to choose Erik (a guy no one even knew existed and was obviously not in the selection), everyone was just cheering and clapping. I don't know about you but if I were watching the Bachelorette and Jojo picked a guy that wasn't even one of her choices and wasn't on the show I'd be like "Who dis bitch". And the media would also go ballistic. But no, everyone was okay with it and didn't think twice.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464142489ra/19202120.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>And then, it was just like "The end, that's it, that's the book". <br><br>And I just sat there like "Wat".<br><br>Yeah, pretty much. I was hoping this book was going to be a good conclusion to the series, but overall, it wrecked it for me. It was so boring. The writing was bad. The characters were flat. The plot was dull. Nothing really happened. <br><br><b>Goodbye forever, Selection series.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464142489ra/19202121.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13500235645060181311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_931692759" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/931692759" />
    <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict"><img alt="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551124421p2/10717098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/931692759?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict">Carol [Goodreads Addict]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=paranormal-fantasy">paranormal-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=royals">royals</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer931692759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16322535038802020438">The Crown is book five in The Selection series by Kiera Cass. This series has captivated me from the beginning. For me, it’s one of the most visual series I’ve ever read. Is it the girly girl in me that loves the gowns, the jewels, the pomp and circumstance? No matter the reason, I’m a fan, and I love the way Kiera Cass wrapped it all up. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464200451i/19211977.jpg' alt='The Crown by Kiera Cass: ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Eadlyn has grown up. This book holds a very different Eadlyn than you met in the beginning. This young woman holds the weight of her country on her shoulders.</span>
  <span id="freeText16322535038802020438" style="display:none">The Crown is book five in The Selection series by Kiera Cass. This series has captivated me from the beginning. For me, it’s one of the most visual series I’ve ever read. Is it the girly girl in me that loves the gowns, the jewels, the pomp and circumstance? No matter the reason, I’m a fan, and I love the way Kiera Cass wrapped it all up. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464200451i/19211977.jpg" alt="The Crown by Kiera Cass: " class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Eadlyn has grown up. This book holds a very different Eadlyn than you met in the beginning. This young woman holds the weight of her country on her shoulders. Her mother lies in the hospital with her husband by her side. Eadlyn has always known the love her parents shared but watching her father at her mother’s side shows her a depth she hadn’t realized. Could she ever have that with one of these men from the Selection? She never even wanted to be a part of this but now finds herself longing for what her parents have. <br><br><b>
  <i>“I had power and no idea how to use it. I was a ruler who didn’t know how to lead. I was a twin who was on her own. I was a daughter with missing parents. I had a half dozen suitors and wasn’t sure how to be in love.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464200451i/19211978._SY540_.jpg" alt="queen: " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Eadlyn is acting as Regent in her father’s absence. She has trained since birth to someday take over the kingdom but she wasn’t prepared for the full responsibility just yet. At the same time, she is somehow trying to find time to get to know the remaining men. She is developing feelings for some of these men but could it be love? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464200451ra/19211979.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Of course, with power, come those that want to take it from you. Someone posing as a friend tries to manipulate Eadlyn and the public to put himself into a place to assume power. With public opinion of Eadlyn less than what she would want it to be, this puts her in a very precarious position. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464200451i/19211980._SY540_.jpg" alt="The Crown Kiera Cass: " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Of course, love can’t be predicted. And for Eadlyn, it came as both a surprise and a shock. But what should have been the most beautiful moment of her life will force her to make a decision that will possible be the biggest sacrifice she will ever make for her kingdom.<br><br><b>
  <i>“In an instant, everything in the room came alive. Like the sunshine had a melody and the sounds of footsteps had a texture I could feel in my fingertips each time anyone moved. The world woke up when I looked at him.”</i>
</b><br><br>Could these feelings just be her own? Or does he feel the same way as well? Does she even dare to voice her feelings or should she keep them locked up inside?<br><br>As I said above, I love this series. I feel like the ending was perfect. Since it’s been awhile since the last book, I don’t remember it being so poetic. Kiera’s way with words in this one was just beautiful. With all the responsibility Eadlyn was forced to take on, I wished she had more time with her gentlemen but in the end, I don’t know if that would have mattered. <br><br>As of late, I’ve gotten away from young adult. But there was no way I couldn’t follow this through to see how it ended. So if you haven’t started this series and are on the fence about it, let me give you a not so gentle nudge and get started. Now there will be no waits between books for you to see what happens next. And if you think of it, let me know how you like it. I hope you enjoy it as much as I have. Thank you to Kiera Cass for such a wonderful, beautiful series.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464200451i/19211981.jpg" alt="Happily Ever After: " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425952445ra/13954015.gif" alt="signature" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16322535038802020438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer6238137062540171571">This is going to go one of two ways.<br/><br/>Way #1: I will love this book. I will gush about this book. I will want to have its children (not really) and pledge my soul to this book (a possibility). <br/><br/>Way #2: I will hate this book so much that I see red. Gouging my eyes out after reading is a possibility (gouging occuring during reading in an [most likely successful] attempt to avoid continuing reading this book is also a possibility, BUT it will only happen if the book is <i>really</i> bad), but I may settle fo</span>
  <span id="freeText6238137062540171571" style="display:none">This is going to go one of two ways.<br /><br />Way #1: I will love this book. I will gush about this book. I will want to have its children (not really) and pledge my soul to this book (a possibility). <br /><br />Way #2: I will hate this book so much that I see red. Gouging my eyes out after reading is a possibility (gouging occuring during reading in an [most likely successful] attempt to avoid continuing reading this book is also a possibility, BUT it will only happen if the book is <i>really</i> bad), but I may settle for minor hair tearing out and extreme ranting.<br /><br />We shall see.</span>

<div id="review_1565099524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1565099524" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1565099524?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1565099524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17883408293061447909"><blockquote>
  <i>“Maybe it's not the first kisses that are supposed to be special. Maybe it's the last ones.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>The Selection : ★★★½<br/>The Elite : ★★★★<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1565629419' rel='nofollow noopener'>The One</a> : ★★★★★<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1643404150' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Heir</a> : ★<br/>The Crown : ★★<br/><br/>Don't mind taking your time with this one. It won't be a review of me ranting about Eadlyn and how stubborn and foolish and rude and spoiled she is. Or was I guess...<br/><br/>I'd like to start off by saying I <b>hated</b> The Heir. I'm sorry, but if you've read my review, you'll know why. If you've read The Heir and were disappointed with it</span>
  <span id="freeText17883408293061447909" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Maybe it's not the first kisses that are supposed to be special. Maybe it's the last ones.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The Selection : ★★★½<br />The Elite : ★★★★<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1565629419" rel="nofollow noopener">The One</a> : ★★★★★<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1643404150" rel="nofollow noopener">The Heir</a> : ★<br />The Crown : ★★<br /><br />Don't mind taking your time with this one. It won't be a review of me ranting about Eadlyn and how stubborn and foolish and rude and spoiled she is. Or was I guess...<br /><br />I'd like to start off by saying I <b>hated</b> The Heir. I'm sorry, but if you've read my review, you'll know why. If you've read The Heir and were disappointed with it, then you'll know why as well. In The Heir, Eadlyn is just rude, stubborn, foolish and spoiled. She has a bitchy attitude and wondered why everyone hated her or had some dislikes of her. But in The Crown, there are some changes.<br /><br />I knew that after reading and finishing The One, the series should've stopped there. It should've stayed as a trilogy. I mean, the main focus was on America and Maxon. Writing 2 stories about their daughter wasn't really worth it. Instead of keeping the happiness flowing everywhere, everything sort of faded because of these 2 other books. Instead of wishing more moments with America and Maxon, we get moments with their daughter and her own selection, even though she didn't want it. Instead of romance, we get boring dates, awkward ones as well, a boring plot, boring main characters and nothing in comparison to <i>The Selection, The Elite and The One.</i><br /><br />I will admit, this story did have its improvements like the other ones did. I mean, in The Heir, a lot of us see Eadlyn as a spoiled brat. I'm sorry, but spoiled explains her a lot in that book. But in The Crown, we notice she makes improvements in her life. She isn't stuck up and spoiled all the time, she doesn't treat everyone like shit, she tries to follow the same moves her father did when he was just a prince, and she shows some care and sympathy for the Selected boys.<br /><br />Nothing really happened in The Crown. There weren't any shocking moments or decisions that were about to leave my jaw hanging open. Honestly, I knew it was all coming. Eadlyn's choice didn't leave me disappointed. I was disappointed since my <i>ship sank and didn't keep floating on the ocean</i> but I didn't completely blame her. Her choice felt right and even though there is no other book coming up, I feel like in the minds of fans of this book can imagine the happy life they'll be living.<br /><br />As to the things that did upset me, even though it's really just one, I think making Eadlyn queen at a young age when both her parents are alive was stupid and ridiculous. Just because your parents are carrying stress on their shoulders and your mom is in a poor condition of recovering, that doesn't mean you give your royal title to your daughter who still doesn't even have a <i>soulmate</i> and doesn't even have a clue on how she would rule the country. Maxon literally gave up on his life to take care of America but then they didn't even know how Eadlyn would handle it. That's just stupid!<br /><br />Other than saying negative things about this book, I was glad Grandma Singer was back, new characters were mentioned and met, and new truths were discovered. I was glad Kiera brought some people back and made some changes in the ones we met in the previous book. I was glad there were character developments although they weren't the best. I don't consider Kiera Cass one of my favorite authors simply because I really only loved The One. I will continue to love that one but only that one. Admittedly, reading her novels are like reading fan fictions. The writing is too cute and written in a quirky way for teenage girls looking for romance that is discovered in a way that is not discovered here. <br /><br />I guess The Selection really is over now. I can't really emphasize the disappointment I was left with this book. I was expecting so much more even though at the same time, I wasn't. The series should've ended with The One. Period. I really hope that if Kiera Cass decides to work on something new, its different. Even if the main genre is romance, I just hope the writing improves and it doesn't just focus on one thing. If she is planning on working on something new for us, I just hope it's worth it and I hope my doubts for it stay high. I'm just hoping. <br /><br />Goodbye Illéa. For real now, and maybe for the best.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17883408293061447909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11906000721369436840"><i>“Maybe it's not the first kisses that are supposed to be special. Maybe it's the last ones.”</i><br/><br/>I have finally finished <i>The Selection</i> series. It was about time.<br/>A few years ago when I read the first book I loved the story. Then came the second book and it went downhill. After <i>The One</i> I passionately hated America. And then I found out that this still wasn't enough and I had to read about her daughter! Who would only be more spoiled and vain and self-centered. If that was even possible.<br/>So why did I kee</span>
  <span id="freeText11906000721369436840" style="display:none"><i>“Maybe it's not the first kisses that are supposed to be special. Maybe it's the last ones.”</i><br /><br />I have finally finished <i>The Selection</i> series. It was about time.<br />A few years ago when I read the first book I loved the story. Then came the second book and it went downhill. After <i>The One</i> I passionately hated America. And then I found out that this still wasn't enough and I had to read about her daughter! Who would only be more spoiled and vain and self-centered. If that was even possible.<br />So why did I keep reading? Two reasons.<br />1. I hate leaving a series unfished.<br />2. <i>The Selection</i> is exactly like the Bachelor. It's crap, but highly entertaining crap.<br /><br /><i>The Crown</i> was no exception. This novel could've been named "The wonderful and great character traits of Eadlyn Schreave". The plot is basically Eadlyn doubting herself, followed by someone telling her how strong she is. Then she doubts herself and someone tells her how strong she is. And, take a guess, then she doubts herself and, yes!, someone tells her how strong she is. I'm not kidding.<br />Apart from that this book had a high level of cheesiness. Which was no big deal, since that's what I was used to from the other books in the series.<br /><br />I'm glad I can take those books from my to-read list and never bother myself with them again.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

<div id="review_1059615534" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1059615534" />
    <a title="Pamela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3645538-pamela"><img alt="Pamela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535386427p2/3645538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1059615534?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamela" href="/user/show/3645538-pamela">Pamela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062458865" href="/book/show/26198897-the-crown">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1059615534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5936173285075358743"><b>**53 people liked this post because of this initial review**</b><br/><br/>OMFG!! YAY <3<br/><br/>lol so much raging in the review section of Goodreads. If you don't like the series why dafaq u stil following it bro? get out & stay out yayy thank you <br/><br/>----------------------------------------<br/><b>**Review of Novel**</b><br/><br/>As I recall, I’ve described Kiera Cass as an author who takes the difficult path and makes it work somehow. She never takes the easy path and this allows her to write interesting storylines and events. I’ve always b</span>
  <span id="freeText5936173285075358743" style="display:none"><b>**53 people liked this post because of this initial review**</b><br /><br />OMFG!! YAY &lt;3<br /><br />lol so much raging in the review section of Goodreads. If you don't like the series why dafaq u stil following it bro? get out &amp; stay out yayy thank you <br /><br />----------------------------------------<br /><b>**Review of Novel**</b><br /><br />As I recall, I’ve described Kiera Cass as an author who takes the difficult path and makes it work somehow. She never takes the easy path and this allows her to write interesting storylines and events. I’ve always been pleasantly surprised by her stories and avidly engaged by her characters. I can describe The Crown using varied words, but good is not one of them.<br /><br />As I began reading this book, I felt that there was something missing. I want to stress that even this early on, I wasn’t planning on rating this book with 5 stars, which is odd for me because I’m an devoted fan of this series. It’s true that the fourth book in the series was a bother to read because of Eadlyn, but I still admired her character. She had a different type of personality, one that a lot of people would not appreciate, but her thoughts and actions made sense when they were strung together. Her personality wasn’t an issue in this book, though. It was evident from the beginning that there were a lot of missing information and that most of the scenes were rushed. There were some scenes where she was suddenly in a date with someone without even an introduction that she was going to one. And said date would end abruptly and nothing interesting actually happens. I understand if this is a tactic to undermine the date, but as readers of Eadlyn’s selection, it also undermines her emotions over her suitors. This, I think, should not have been done because she repeats every now and then that she cares deeply for them – even going so far as to say that she loves all of them. The lack of focus on the dates make these claims easily refutable.<br /><br />There was also a huge deficiency in character development. There were certain things in the book that were revealed rather abruptly. If you think about it, the clipped dates should have given way to more space for the development of other aspects of the story, but it didn’t. These revelations caused so much turmoil in me that I was unable to continue right away. I was so pissed! I never curse in reviews, but that development was COMPLETE BULLSHIT. I’m not really picky when it comes to characters, as long as there’s evidence of how so and so could have happened, I’m okay with it. And yes, there were scenes that could have lead up to that kind of development, but EADLYN WASN’T IN THAT STATE OF EMOTION. AT ALL.<br /><br />I can’t… this book is a MAJOR DISAPPOINTMET.<br /><br />I love the America &amp; Maxon moments, but if Kiera Cass really needed more space for character development, then they should have just cut out these scenes from the book. HELL, I would have preferred another book if that would let me avoid this mess of a rushed book. I’m thoroughly disappointed. I tried to see how what happened had happened (avoiding spoilers is hard, whew!) but I just couldn’t. I even tried to accept it, like – okay, you can’t do anything anymore, this is the flow of the story. But I was at such at an emotional disconnect by that point that I couldn’t enjoy the story anymore.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The Marid plotline was so obvious that I can’t believe Eadlyn missed it. And she only started to take notice of it when she was drunk! Also, I’m not sure what constitutional monarchy entails, but by voting for a prime minister, it would appear that with Marid’s popularity, he could still get the position if he so wanted. This book, I tell you, is complete BULLSHIT. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Kiera, if you’re reading this or if this somehow gets to you, please understand that I’m not against your decisions. However, I AM mad that things were too abrupt, had no buildups, and seemed to have little to no thought put into it. It's obvious; this book didn’t even reach 300 pages. Everything was sloppy, even the writing style. I’ve read better self-published novels than this.<br /><br />This is a very, VERY harsh review, I know, but I loved the Selection series because of how emotional everything was and because I was able to sympathize with the characters. I didn’t love this series because of sloppiness or laziness from the author’s part. I know that Eadlyn isn’t supposed to be a very emotional person, but everyone – and I do mean EVERYONE, no matter how cold and stoic they appear in everyday life – does not stay that way when presented with emotional situations. Especially people who are self-centered, which Eadlyn proclaims to be. Self-centered people are concerned with everything about them including their feelings, ESPECIALLY THEIR FEELINGS, no matter how calculating they may seem. But no, Eadlyn was portrayed as someone who wanted to be the best monarch for her people and was despised despite her efforts. This is not being self-centered. This is attempting to make your character do things that your fans would want her to do. This is making your character make choices that she isn’t prepared to do yet in that part of the book. This is BASTARDIZING your story by forcing it to end by page 278.<br /><br />I won’t even end this review with a proper conclusion. We didn’t get one, why should this?</span>
  <a data-text-id="5936173285075358743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I found it boring and the romance was so rushed and came out of the blue. By halfway through the author still had me guessing on who Eadlyn, our stupid useless heroine, would choose. She had guys coming from far and wide just for her to "pick". Load of bull. I just taught Eadlyn's story was pointless. I am sure these two books would have been so much better if Maxon and America's story had continued from book 3 </span>
  <span id="freeText15048475764340954797" style="display:none">Minor spoilers<br /><br />Major rant<br /><br />So I read through this in one sitting but I did not like it. <div id="review_1485691933" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1485691933" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1485691933?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=21th-century">21th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1485691933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer499326637932725593">The Crown (The Selection #5), Kiera Cass<br/><br/>Twenty years have passed since America Singer and Prince Maxon fell in love, and their daughter is the first princess to hold a Selection of her own. <br/><br/>Eadlyn didn't think she would find a real partner among the Selection's thirty-five suitors, let alone true love. But sometimes the heart has a way of surprising you, and now Eadlyn must make a choice that feels more difficult-and more important-than she ever expected.<br/><br/>تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز نوزدهم ماه نوامبر</span>
  <span id="freeText499326637932725593" style="display:none">The Crown (The Selection #5), Kiera Cass<br /><br />Twenty years have passed since America Singer and Prince Maxon fell in love, and their daughter is the first princess to hold a Selection of her own. <br /><br />Eadlyn didn't think she would find a real partner among the Selection's thirty-five suitors, let alone true love. But sometimes the heart has a way of surprising you, and now Eadlyn must make a choice that feels more difficult-and more important-than she ever expected.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز نوزدهم ماه نوامبر سال 2017 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: تاج: کتاب پنجم از سری گزینش (انتخاب)؛ نویسنده: کایرا کاس؛ برگردان: رباب پورعسگر؛ تهران، نشر بهداد، 1395؛ در ؟ ص؛ شابک: 9786008203650؛ موضوع داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی - سده 21م<br /><br />در جلد پنجم از سری «انتخاب» با عنوان «تاج»، دوره‌ ی تازه ای در دنیای رقابت «انتخاب» آغاز شد؛ از زمانیکه «امریکا سینگر» و «شاهزاده مکسون» عاشق هم شدند، و ازدواج کردند، بیست سال بگذشته است، و اکنون دخترشان نخستین شاهدختی است، که رقابت «انتخاب» را تجربه می‌کند؛ «ایدلن» خیال نمی‌کرد، بتواند بین سی و پنج خواستگارش، یک شریک زندگی واقعی پیدا کند، چه برسد به اینکه عشق واقعی خویش را بیابد؛ ولی گاهی قلب آدمی، او را غافلگیر می‌کند...؛ و حالا نوبت «ایدلن» است، تا دست به انتخابی بزند، که اکنون دشوارتر– و مهم‌تر– از حد انتظارش است؛<br /><br />نقل نمونه متن:(خودم را آماده ی هر نوع واکنش اجتناب ناپذیری کردم، و گفتم: «متاسفم.» وقتی رقابت انتخابِ مخصوص من شروع شد، در ذهنم پایانش را اینطور تجسم کرده بودم؛ ده ها نفر از خواستگارهایم یکباره حذف میشوند، و بیشترشان آمادگی خروج از دور رقابت، و از دست دادن توجه مردم را ندارند؛ ولی در هفته های اخیر که پی بردم بسیاری از آنها صاحب شخصیتی مهربان، باهوش و سخاوتمند بودند، به این نتیجه رسیدم که حذف دسته جمعی آنها مایه ی دل شکستگی من میشود.؛ پسرها رفتاری عادلانه با من داشتند، و الان مجبور بودم خیلی غیرمنصفانه با آنها برخورد کنم.؛ - میدونم غیرمنتظره ست ولی با در نظر گرفتن شرایط خطرناک مادرم، پدرم از من خواسته، مسئولیت بیشتری به عهده بگیرم، و حس میکنم تنها راه پیش بردن این روند، کاهش تدریجی شرکت کننده های رقابته.؛ ایوان آب دهانش را به سختی قورت داد و پرسید: «حال ملکه چطوره؟» آه کشیدم.؛ «مادرم...، حالش خیلی خوب نیست.»؛ پدرم مردد بود، که به من اجازه ی دیدن مادرم را بدهد، ولی بالاخره او را متقاعد کرده بودم.؛ لحظه ای که چشمم به مادرم افتاد، متوجه دلیل بی میلی پدرم شدم؛ مادرم خوابیده بود، و میزان ضربان قلبش روی نمایشگر عددی مشخص را نشان میداد.؛ او را تازه از عمل جراحی آورده و دکترها مجبور شده بودند، رگی از پایش جدا کرده، و جایگزین رگی در سینه اش بکنند که از کار افتاده بود.؛ یکی از دکترها گفت ضربان قلب مادرم دقایقی قطع شده بود، ولی موفق شده بودند، دوباره او را به زندگی برگردانند.؛ کنار مادرم نشستم، و دستش را گرفتم.؛ احمقانه به نظر می رسید، روی صندلی با بیحالی نشسته بودم، و یقین داشتم با اینکارم هوشیاریش را به دست میآورد، بلند میشود و به من میگوید درست بنشینم؛ خیالی واهی بود.؛ ولی زنده ست و پدرم...؛ اون...؛ «رائول» برای دلگرمی دادن، دستش را روی شانه ام گذاشت، و گفت «اشکالی نداره، علیاحضرت.؛ همه ی ما این موقعیت رو درک میکنیم.»؛ فضای آنجا را از نظر گذراندم و به تک تک خواستگارهایم زل زدم، تا نیرو بگیرم، و چهره شان را به خاطر بسپارم.»؛ پایان نقل<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 14/05/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="499326637932725593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2026779349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10287787106281684785">*THIS BOOK WAS NOT OKAY FOR MY BRAIN AND I"M JUST GOING TO START OFF BY RANTING.*<br/><br/>So, as you can see, my brain can't work for two reasons-<br/>Number one: This book was just TERRIBLE. I just.....I can't......<br/>And...<br/>Number 2: It's 10:30 in the morning and we all know for lazy teens like me, I need my beauty rest but I just couldn't lay my ass down in bed and do nothing, SO HERE I AM.<br/><br/>Now, with my little update of my miserable life, here i go.<br/>Eadlyn was just this little, immature, ungrateful child. And I </span>
  <span id="freeText10287787106281684785" style="display:none">*THIS BOOK WAS NOT OKAY FOR MY BRAIN AND I"M JUST GOING TO START OFF BY RANTING.*<br /><br />So, as you can see, my brain can't work for two reasons-<br />Number one: This book was just TERRIBLE. I just.....I can't......<br />And...<br />Number 2: It's 10:30 in the morning and we all know for lazy teens like me, I need my beauty rest but I just couldn't lay my ass down in bed and do nothing, SO HERE I AM.<br /><br />Now, with my little update of my miserable life, here i go.<br />Eadlyn was just this little, immature, ungrateful child. And I know, she does have her good points, but straight off the bat, she talks about how she's all important, yet she doesn't want to be. I mean, she literally starts complaining in the book before this!!<br /><br />Besides this, the romance was just trash! <br />Why'd she pick the other dude??!!<br />I swear, she barely even knew him, and then all of a sudden, she's like, "Oh! He's the one for me!!"<br />*swoon*<br />I DON"T EVEN KNOW HOW IT WORKED. <br />How does the author build up so much between her and mystery dude in a few pages??!! How does Eadlyn suddenly find this random guy so hot, and so charming, and so blah-de-blah-blah??!!<br /><br />To be honest, the romance was probably the biggest thing that screwed up this story. So warning for y'all, don't read this if you're in a cranky mood, because your computer will break as you slowly let all your anger pour out into reviews....<br /><br />*sniffle* My poor keyboard.....<br /><br />Read it if ya want!! But I suggest the first three books are all that you need!!<br /><br />now i need food......</span>
